All were joint projects with the conservative group <a href="/wiki/Citizens_United_(organization)" title="Citizens United (organization)">Citizens United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secret_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-secret-120">[120]</a></sup> In 2011, Newt and Callista appeared in <i>A City Upon a Hill</i>, on the subject of <a href="/wiki/American_exceptionalism" title="American exceptionalism">American exceptionalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of May 2011, the company had about five employees. In 2010, it paid Gingrich more than $2.4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-net_worth_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-net_worth-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gingrich_Communications">Gingrich Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Gingrich Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Gingrich Communications promoted Gingrich's public appearances, including his <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> contract and his website, newt.org.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-small_business_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-small_business-114">[114]</a></sup> Gingrich received as much as $60,000 for a speech, and did as many as 80 in a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inc_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-Inc-109">[109]</a></sup> One of Gingrich's nonprofit groups, Renewing American Leadership, which was founded in March 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secret_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-secret-120">[120]</a></sup> paid Gingrich Communications $220,000 over two years; the charity shared the names of its donors with Gingrich, who could use them for his for-profit companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Gingrich Communications, which employed 15 people at its largest, closed in 2011 when Gingrich began his presidential campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-small_business_114-3"><a href="#cite_note-small_business-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Celebrity Leaders is a booking agency that handled Gingrich's speaking engagements, as well as those other clients such as former Republican National Committee chair <a href="/wiki/Michael_Steele" title="Michael Steele">Michael Steele</a> and former Pennsylvania Senator <a href="/wiki/Rick_Santorum" title="Rick Santorum">Rick Santorum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-house_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-house-108">[108]</a></sup> Kathy Lubbers, the President and CEO of the agency,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> who is Gingrich's daughter, owns the agency. Gingrich has shares in the agency, and was paid more than $70,000 by it in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li>FGH Publications handles the production of and royalties from fiction books co-authored by Gingrich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-small_business_114-4"><a href="#cite_note-small_business-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_activity">Political activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Political activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg/220px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg/330px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg/440px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_9.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gingrich addressing the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Political_Action_Conference" title="Conservative Political Action Conference">Conservative Political Action Conference</a> (CPAC)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 2005 and 2007, Gingrich expressed interest in running for the 2008 Republican presidential nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> On October 13, 2005, Gingrich suggested he was considering a run for president, saying, "There are circumstances where I will run", elaborating that those circumstances would be if no other candidate champions some of the platform ideas he advocates. On September 28, 2007, Gingrich announced that if his supporters pledged $30 million to his campaign by October 21, he would seek the nomination.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>However, insisting that he had "pretty strongly" considered running,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> on September 29 spokesman Rick Tyler said that Gingrich would not seek the presidency in 2008 because he could not continue to serve as chairman of American Solutions if he did so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Citing campaign finance law restrictions (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McCain-Feingold" title="McCain-Feingold">McCain-Feingold</a> campaign law would have forced him to leave his American Solutions political organization if he declared his candidacy), Gingrich said, "I wasn't prepared to abandon American Solutions, even to explore whether a campaign was realistic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2009 special election in New York's 23rd congressional district, Gingrich endorsed moderate Republican candidate <a href="/wiki/Dede_Scozzafava" title="Dede Scozzafava">Dede Scozzafava</a>, rather than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_New_York" title="Conservative Party of New York">Conservative Party</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Doug_Hoffman" title="Doug Hoffman">Doug Hoffman</a>, who had been endorsed by several nationally prominent Republicans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> He was heavily criticized for this endorsement, with conservatives questioning his candidacy for President in 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and even comparing him to <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Arnold" title="Benedict Arnold">Benedict Arnold</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Gingrich has since regretted his decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_presidential_campaign">2012 presidential campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2012 presidential campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newt_Gingrich_presidential_campaign,_2012" title="Newt Gingrich presidential campaign, 2012">Newt Gingrich presidential campaign, 2012</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012,_UNEDITED._(6854524645).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg/220px-Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg/330px-Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg/440px-Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012%2C_UNEDITED._%286854524645%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_Speaking_at_CPAC_2012,_UNEDITED._(6854524645).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Newt Gingrich Speaking at CPAC in February 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In late 2008 several political commentators, including <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ambinder" title="Marc Ambinder">Marc Ambinder</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Novak" title="Robert Novak">Robert Novak</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> identified Gingrich as a top presidential contender in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012 election</a>, with Ambinder reporting that Gingrich was "already planting some seeds in <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>". A July 2010 poll conducted by Public Policy Polling indicated that Gingrich was the leading GOP contender for the Republican nomination with 23% of likely Republican voters saying they would vote for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Describing his views as a possible candidate during an appearance on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/On_the_Record_w/_Greta_Van_Susteren" title="On the Record w/ Greta Van Susteren">On the Record</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Greta_Van_Susteren" title="Greta Van Susteren">Greta Van Susteren</a> in March 2009, Gingrich said, "I am very sad that a number of Republicans do not understand that this country is sick of <a href="/wiki/Earmark_(politics)" title="Earmark (politics)">earmarks</a>. [Americans] are sick of politicians taking care of themselves. They are sick of their money being spent in a way that is absolutely indefensible ... I think you're going to see a steady increase in the number of incumbents who have opponents because the American taxpayers are increasingly fed up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 3, 2011, Gingrich officially announced a website entitled "Newt Exploratory 2012" in lieu of a formal <a href="/wiki/Exploratory_committee" title="Exploratory committee">exploratory committee</a> for exploration of a potential presidential run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> On May 11, 2011, Gingrich officially announced his intention to seek the GOP nomination in 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On June 9, 2011, a group of Gingrich's senior campaign aides left the campaign en masse, leading to doubts about the viability of his presidential run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> On June 21, 2011, two more senior aides left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response, Gingrich stated that he had not quit the race for the Republican nomination, and pointed to his experience running for 5 years to win his seat in Congress, spending 16 years helping to build a Republican majority in the house and working for decades to build a Republican majority in Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Some commentators noted Gingrich's resilience throughout his career, in particular with regards to his presidential campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg/220px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg/330px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg/440px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gingrich at a political conference during his 2012 presidential bid, in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After then-front-runner <a href="/wiki/Herman_Cain" title="Herman Cain">Herman Cain</a> was damaged by allegations of past <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, Gingrich gained support, and quickly became a contender in the race, especially after Cain suspended his campaign. By December 4, 2011, Gingrich was leading in the national polls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> However, after an abundance of negative ads run by his opponents throughout December, Gingrich's national polling lead had fallen to a tie with <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 3, 2012, Gingrich finished in fourth place in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iowa_Republican_caucuses,_2012" title="Iowa Republican caucuses, 2012">Iowa Republican caucuses</a>, far behind <a href="/wiki/Rick_Santorum" title="Rick Santorum">Rick Santorum</a>, Romney, and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul" title="Ron Paul">Ron Paul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iowaresults_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-iowaresults-147">[147]</a></sup> On January 10, Gingrich finished in fifth place in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Republican_primary,_2012" title="New Hampshire Republican primary, 2012">New Hampshire Republican primary</a>, far behind Romney, Santorum, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jon_Huntsman,_Jr." title="Jon Huntsman, Jr.">Jon Huntsman</a>, and Paul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the field narrowed with the withdrawal from the race of Huntsman and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a>, Gingrich won the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Republican_primary,_2012" title="South Carolina Republican primary, 2012">Republican primary</a> on January 21, obtaining about 40% of the vote, considerably ahead of Romney, Santorum and Paul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> This surprise victory allowed Gingrich to reemerge as the frontrunner once again heading into Florida.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On January 31, 2012, Gingrich placed second in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Republican_primary,_2012" title="Florida Republican primary, 2012">Republican Florida primary</a>, losing by a fifteen percentage point margin, 47% to 32%. Some factors that contributed to this outcome include two strong debate performances by Romney (which were typically Gingrich's strong suit), the wide margin by which the Gingrich campaign was outspent in television ads,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> and a widely criticized proposal by Gingrich to have a permanent colony on the moon by 2020 to reinvigorate the American Space Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was later revealed Romney had hired a debate coach to help him perform better in the Florida debates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gingrich did, however, significantly outvote Santorum and Paul. On February 4, 2012, Gingrich placed a distant second in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nevada_Republican_caucuses,_2012" title="Nevada Republican caucuses, 2012">Nevada Republican caucuses</a> with 21%, losing to Romney who received over 50% of the total votes cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COUNTY_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-COUNTY-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 7, 2012, Gingrich came in last place in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minnesota_Republican_caucuses,_2012" title="Minnesota Republican caucuses, 2012">Minnesota Republican caucuses</a> with about 10.7% of the vote. Santorum won the caucus, followed by Paul and Romney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-startribune020812_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-startribune020812-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/Super_Tuesday" title="Super Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a> Gingrich won his home state, Georgia, which has the most delegates, in "an otherwise dismal night for him". Santorum took Tennessee and Oklahoma, where Gingrich had previously performed well in the polls, though Gingrich managed a statistical second place showing in Oklahoma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newt_SUPER_TUESDAY_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newt_SUPER_TUESDAY-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 4, the Rick Santorum campaign shifted its position and urged Gingrich to drop out of the race and support Santorum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 10, Santorum announced the suspension of his campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Following this announcement, The Newt 2012 campaign used a new slogan referring to Gingrich as "the last conservative standing". Despite this, on April 19, Gingrich told Republicans in New York that he would work to help Romney win the general election if Romney secured the nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a disappointing second place showing in the Delaware primary on April 24, and with a campaign debt in excess of $4 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes04272012_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes04272012-162">[162]</a></sup> Gingrich suspended his campaign and endorsed front-runner Mitt Romney on May 2, 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> on whose behalf he subsequently campaigned (i.e. stump speeches and television appearances).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Gingrich later hosted a number of policy workshops at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Republican_National_Convention" title="2012 Republican National Convention">GOP Convention in Tampa</a> presented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Republican_Committee" title="National Republican Committee">National Republican Committee</a> called "Newt University".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> He and his wife Calista addressed the convention on its final day with a Ronald Reagan-themed introduction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2016, Newt Gingrich filed a debt settlement plan document with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Election_Commission" title="Federal Election Commission">Federal Election Commission</a> indicating his 2012 presidential campaign would pay zero dollars toward the more than $4.6 million in unpaid debts owed to 114 businesses and consultants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Donald_Trump_presidential_campaign">2016 Donald Trump presidential campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2016 Donald Trump presidential campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_campaign_of_Donald_Trump,_2016" title="Presidential campaign of Donald Trump, 2016">Presidential campaign of Donald Trump, 2016</a></div>
<p>After having consulted for <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s 2016 campaign, Gingrich encouraged his fellow Republicans to unify behind Trump, who had by then become the presumptive Republican presidential nominee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Gingrich reportedly figured among Trump's final three choices to be his running mate;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VP_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-VP-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> the position ultimately went to <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pence" title="Mike Pence">Mike Pence</a>, a politician known for his role as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Indiana" title="Governor of Indiana">Governor of Indiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following Trump's victory in the presidential election, speculation arose concerning Gingrich as a possible Secretary of State, or Chief of Staff, or advisor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Eventually, Gingrich announced that he would not be serving in the cabinet. He stated that he didn't have the interest in serving in any role related to the Trump administration, stressing that as a private citizen he would engage with individuals for "strategic planning" rather than job-seeking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McClatchyDC_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchyDC-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_positions">Political positions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Political positions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_positions_of_Newt_Gingrich" title="Political positions of Newt Gingrich">Political positions of Newt Gingrich</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg/220px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg/330px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg/440px-Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newt_Gingrich_by_Gage_Skidmore_11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gingrich in 2014, addressing a group of conservatives</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_(R-Calif.)_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_(JSA)_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1928" data-file-width="2910" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg/220px-Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg/330px-Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg/440px-Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_%28R-Calif.%29_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_%28JSA%29_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Speaker_of_the_House_Newt_Gingrich_and_Congressman_Jay_Kim_(R-Calif.)_face_North_Korea_from_the_Joint_Security_Area_(JSA)_A1501-SCN-97-0027-003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Speaker Newt Gingrich, Congressman <a href="/wiki/Jay_Kim" title="Jay Kim">Jay Kim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Royce" title="Ed Royce">Ed Royce</a> (R-Calif.) face <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Security_Area" title="Joint Security Area">Joint Security Area</a> in 1997</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gingrich is most widely identified with the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Contract_with_America" title="Contract with America">Contract with America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> He is a founder of <a href="/wiki/American_Solutions_for_Winning_the_Future" title="American Solutions for Winning the Future">American Solutions for Winning the Future</a>. More recently, Gingrich has advocated replacing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> with a proposed "Environmental Solutions Agency".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>He favors a strong immigration border policy and a <a href="/wiki/Guest_worker_program" title="Guest worker program">guest worker program</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> In terms of energy policy, he's argued in favor of <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flex-fuel</a> mandates for cars sold in the U.S. and promoted the use of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a> generally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adler_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adler-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gingrich has taken a diminutive view of <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">internationalism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. He said in 2015, "after several years of looking at the UN, I can report to you that it is sufficiently corrupt and sufficiently inefficient. That no reasonable person would put faith in it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Gingrich authored a book, <i><a href="/wiki/Rediscovering_God_in_America" title="Rediscovering God in America">Rediscovering God in America</a></i>, arguing that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers" title="Founding Fathers">Founding Fathers</a> actively intended the new republic to not only allow, but encourage, religious expression in the public square.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Following publication of the book, he was invited by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Falwell" title="Jerry Falwell">Jerry Falwell</a> to be the speaker for the second time at Liberty University's graduation, on May 19, 2007, due to Gingrich having "dedicated much of his time to calling [the United States of] America back to our Christian heritage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsmaxfalwell_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsmaxfalwell-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gingrich's later books take a large-scale policy focus, including <i>Winning the Future</i>, and the most recent, <i><a href="/wiki/To_Save_America" title="To Save America">To Save America</a></i>. Gingrich has identified education as "the number one factor in our future prosperity", and has partnered with <a href="/wiki/Al_Sharpton" title="Al Sharpton">Al Sharpton</a> and Education Secretary <a href="/wiki/Arne_Duncan" title="Arne Duncan">Arne Duncan</a> on education issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Although he previously opposed gay marriage, in December 2012 Gingrich suggested that Republicans should reconsider their opposition to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 14, 2016, Gingrich stated that he believes that Americans of Muslim backgrounds who believe in Sharia law should be deported, and that visiting websites that promote the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> or <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> should be a felony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Some observers have questioned whether these views violate the free speech and free exercise of religion clauses of the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 21, 2016, Gingrich argued that members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> "ought to worry" about a U.S. commitment to their defense. He expanded, saying, "They ought to worry about commitment under any circumstances. Every president has been saying that the NATO countries do not pay their fair share". He also stated that, in the context of whether the United States would provide aid to Estonia (a NATO member) in the event of a Russian invasion, he "would think about it a great deal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 7, 2016, the 75th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, Gingrich was condemned by many after he tweeted that "75 years ago the Japanese displayed professional brilliance and technological power launching surprises from Hawaii to the Philippines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages_and_children">Marriages and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Marriages and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gingrich has married three times. In 1962, he married Jacqueline May "Jackie" Battley (February 21, 1936 – August 7, 2013), his former high school <a href="/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">geometry</a> teacher, when he was 19 years old and she was 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> They have two daughters from their marriage: Kathy Gingrich Lubbers, married to Paul Lubbers, is president of Gingrich Communications,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and Jackie Gingrich Cushman, the wife of Jimmy Cushman, Jr., is an author, conservative columnist, and political commentator,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> whose books include <i>5 Principles for a Successful Life</i>, co-authored with Newt Gingrich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the spring of 1980, Gingrich left his wife after beginning an affair with Marianne Ginther.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1984, Jackie Battley Gingrich told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> that the divorce was a "complete surprise" to her. According to Jackie, in September 1980, Gingrich and their children visited her while she was in the hospital, recovering from surgery for cancer, and Gingrich wanted to discuss the terms of their divorce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Gingrich has disputed that account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-191">[191]</a></sup> In 2011, their daughter, Jackie Gingrich Cushman, stated it was her mother who requested the divorce, that it happened prior to the hospital stay, and that Gingrich's visit was for the purpose of bringing the couple's children to see their mother, not to discuss the divorce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Although Gingrich's presidential campaign staff continued to insist in 2011 that his wife requested the divorce, court documents obtained by <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> from <a href="/wiki/Carroll_County,_Georgia" title="Carroll County, Georgia">Carroll County, Georgia</a>, indicated that Jackie had asked a judge to block the process stating that although "she has adequate and ample grounds for divorce ... she does not desire one at this time [and] does not admit that this marriage is irretrievably broken."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> The daughter of the former Linda May Clay and Wilbur Allen Battley, Jackie Gingrich was a native of <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Georgia" title="Columbus, Georgia">Columbus, Georgia</a>. She was a <a href="/wiki/Deacon" title="Deacon">deacon</a> and active volunteer in the First Baptist Church of <a href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Georgia" title="Carrollton, Georgia">Carrollton, Georgia</a>. She died in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta</a> at the age of 77.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg/220px-Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg/330px-Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg/440px-Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newt_%26_Callista_Gingrich.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gingrich alongside wife <a href="/wiki/Callista_Gingrich" title="Callista Gingrich">Callista</a> at a townhall in <a href="/wiki/Derry,_New_Hampshire" title="Derry, New Hampshire">Derry, New Hampshire</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to L. H. Carter, Gingrich's campaign treasurer, Gingrich said of his first wife: "She's not young enough or pretty enough to be the wife of the President. And besides, she has cancer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Gingrich has denied saying it. His supporters dismiss Carter as a disgruntled former aide who was miffed at not being asked to accompany Gingrich to Washington.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981, six months after his divorce from his first wife was final, Gingrich wed Marianne Ginther.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blogs.cbn.com_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.cbn.com-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Marianne helped control their finances to get them out of debt. She was also coauthor of his 1984 book <i>Window of Opportunity: A Blueprint for the Future</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> She did not, however, want to have the public life of a politician's wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanity_Fair_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vanity_Fair-203">[203]</a></sup> Gingrich's daughter Kathy Lubbers described the marriage as "difficult".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, while still married to Marianne, Gingrich began an affair with House of Representatives staffer <a href="/wiki/Callista_Gingrich" title="Callista Gingrich">Callista Bisek</a>, more thas two decades his junior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> Gingrich and his second wife were divorced in 2000. The marriage produced no children. On January 19, 2012, Marianne Ginther Gingrich alleged in an interview on ABC's <i>Nightline</i> that she had declined to accept Gingrich's suggestion of an <a href="/wiki/Open_marriage" title="Open marriage">open marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTOpen_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTOpen-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>Asked about the allegations at the beginning of the televised South Carolina primary debate, Gingrich said the story was false and told moderator <a href="/wiki/John_King_(journalist)" title="John King (journalist)">John King</a> that making an ex-wife a significant question in a presidential campaign was "close to despicable." Gingrich received a <a href="/wiki/Standing_ovation" title="Standing ovation">standing ovation</a> for parlaying a personal scandal into an attack on what he perceived as <a href="/wiki/Media_bias_in_the_United_States#Liberal_bias" title="Media bias in the United States">biased media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2000, Gingrich married Callista Bisek four months after his divorce from Marianne was finalized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> He and Callista live in <a href="/wiki/McLean,_Virginia" title="McLean, Virginia">McLean, Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In a 2011 interview with David Brody of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Broadcasting_Network" title="Christian Broadcasting Network">Christian Broadcasting Network</a>, Gingrich addressed his past infidelities by saying, "There's no question at times in my life, partially driven by how passionately I felt about this country, that I worked too hard and things happened in my life that were not appropriate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blogs.cbn.com_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.cbn.com-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-201">[201]</a></sup> In December 2011, after the group Iowans for Christian Leaders in Government requested that he sign their so-called "Marriage Vow", Gingrich sent a lengthy written response. It included his pledge to "uphold personal fidelity to my spouse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raised as a Lutheran,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> Gingrich was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist" title="Southern Baptist">Southern Baptist</a> in graduate school. He converted to <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a>, Bisek's faith, on March 29, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GetReligion.org_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-GetReligion.org-212">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> He said: "over the course of several years, I gradually became Catholic and then decided one day to accept the faith I had already come to embrace". He decided to officially become a Catholic when he saw <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>, during the Pope's <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI%27s_visit_to_the_United_States" title="Pope Benedict XVI's visit to the United States">visit to the United States in 2008</a>: "Catching a glimpse of Pope Benedict that day, I was struck by the happiness and peacefulness he exuded. The joyful and radiating presence of the Holy Father was a moment of confirmation about the many things I had been thinking and experiencing for several years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> At a 2011 appearance in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>, he said, "In America, religious belief is being challenged by a cultural elite trying to create a secularized America, in which God is driven out of public life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zeleny226_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zeleny226-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gingrich is allowed to receive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Communion" title="Holy Communion">Holy Communion</a>, despite being divorced, because the Catholic Church has annulled his two earlier marriages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_interests">Other interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Other interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gingrich has written about his interest in animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Gingrich's first engagement in civic affairs was speaking to the city council in his native <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">Harrisburg, Pennsylvania</a>, as to why the city should establish its own zoo.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>He wrote the introduction to <i>America's Best Zoos</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> He is also a <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a> enthusiast. The <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">New Yorker</a></i> said of his 1995 book <i>To Renew America</i>: "Charmingly, he has retained his enthusiasm for the extinct giants into middle age. In addition to including breakthroughs in dinosaur research on his list of futuristic wonders, he specified 'people interested in dinosaurs' as a prime example of who might benefit from his education proposals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">Space exploration</a> has been an interest since his fascination with the United States/Soviet Union <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a> during his teenage years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aviation_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation-222">[222]</a></sup> Gingrich wants the U.S. to pursue new achievements in space, such as sustaining civilizations beyond Earth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> but advocates relying more on the private sector and less on the publicly funded <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> to drive progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2010, he has served on the <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Society" title="National Space Society">National Space Society</a> Board of Governors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2012 election campaign, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artinfo" title="Artinfo">Artinfo</a></i> noted that Gingrich has expressed appreciation for the work of two American painters. He has described <a href="/wiki/James_H._Cromartie" title="James H. Cromartie">James H. Cromartie</a>'s painting of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Capitol" title="U.S. Capitol">U.S. Capitol</a> as "an exceptional and truly beautiful work of art"; in <a href="/wiki/Norman_Rockwell" title="Norman Rockwell">Norman Rockwell</a>'s work, he saw the embodiment of an America circa 1965, at odds with the prevailing sentiment of the modern day "cultural elites".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> announced on June 26, 2013, that Gingrich would join a new version of <i><a href="/wiki/Crossfire_(TV_series)" title="Crossfire (TV series)">Crossfire</a></i> re-launching in fall 2013, with panelists <a href="/wiki/S._E._Cupp" title="S. E. Cupp">S. E. Cupp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Cutter" title="Stephanie Cutter">Stephanie Cutter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Van_Jones" title="Van Jones">Van Jones</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xfire_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-xfire-227">[227]</a></sup> Gingrich represented the <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right</a> on the revamped debate program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xfire_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-xfire-227">[227]</a></sup> The show was cancelled the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Books_and_film">Books and film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Books and film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nonfiction">Nonfiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Nonfiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gingrich has authored or co-authored 18 non-fiction books since 1982.</p>
<div class="refbegin columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><i>The Government's Role in Solving Societal Problems</i>, Associated Faculty Press, Incorporated. January 1982 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780867330267">ISBN 978-0-86733-026-7</a></li>
<li><i>Window of Opportunity</i>. Tom Doherty Associates, December 1985. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312939236">ISBN 978-0-312-93923-6</a></li>
<li><i>Contract with America</i> (co-editor). Times Books, December 1994. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780812925869">ISBN 978-0-8129-2586-9</a></li>
<li><i>Restoring the Dream</i>. Times Books, May 1995. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780812926668">ISBN 978-0-8129-2666-8</a></li>
<li><i>Quotations from Speaker Newt</i>. Workman Publishing Company, Inc., July 1995. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780761100928">ISBN 978-0-7611-0092-8</a></li>
<li><i>To Renew America</i>. Farrar Straus &amp; Giroux, July 1996. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780061095399">ISBN 978-0-06-109539-9</a></li>
<li><i>Lessons Learned The Hard Way</i>. HarperCollins Publishers, May 1998 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780060191061">ISBN 978-0-06-019106-1</a></li>
<li><i>Presidential Determination Regarding Certification of the Thirty-Two Major Illicit Narcotics Producing and Transit Countries</i>. DIANE Publishing Company, September 1999. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780788131868">ISBN 978-0-7881-3186-8</a></li>
<li><i>Saving Lives and Saving Money</i>. <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville_Institution" title="Alexis de Tocqueville Institution">Alexis de Tocqueville Institution</a>, April 2003. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780970548542">ISBN 978-0-9705485-4-2</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Winning_the_Future" title="Winning the Future">Winning the Future</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Regnery_Publishing" title="Regnery Publishing">Regnery Publishing</a>, January 2005. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780895260420">ISBN 978-0-89526-042-0</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Rediscovering_God_in_America" title="Rediscovering God in America">Rediscovering God in America</a>: Reflections on the Role of Faith in Our Nation's History and Future</i>, Integrity Publishers, October 2006. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781591454823">ISBN 978-1-59145-482-3</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Transformation" title="The Art of Transformation">The Art of Transformation</a></i>, with Nancy Desmond. CHT Press, November 29, 2006, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781933966007">ISBN 978-1-933966-00-7</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Contract_with_the_Earth" title="A Contract with the Earth">A Contract with the Earth</a></i>, with Terry L. Maple. <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>, October 1, 2007. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780801887802">ISBN 978-0-8018-8780-2</a></li>
<li><i>Real Change: From the World That Fails to the World That Works</i>, Regnery Publishing, January 2008. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781596980532">ISBN 978-1-59698-053-2</a></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drill_Here._Drill_Now." title="Drill Here. Drill Now.">Drill Here, Drill Now, Pay Less: A Handbook for Slashing Gas Prices and Solving Our Energy Crisis</a></i>, with Vince Haley. Regnery Publishing, September 2008 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781596985766">ISBN 978-1-59698-576-6</a></li>
<li><i>5 Principles for a Successful Life: From Our Family to Yours</i>, with Jackie Gingrich Cushman, Crown Publishing Group, May 2009 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780307462329">ISBN 978-0-307-46232-9</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/To_Save_America" title="To Save America">To Save America</a>: Stopping Obama's Secular-Socialist Machine</i>, with Joe DeSantis. Regnery Publishing, May 2010 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781596985964">ISBN 978-1-59698-596-4</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Nation_Like_No_Other" title="A Nation Like No Other">A Nation Like No Other</a>: Why American Exceptionalism Matters</i>, Regnery Publishing, June 2011 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781596982710">ISBN 978-1-59698-271-0</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiction">Fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newt_Gingrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gingrich co-wrote the following <a href="/wiki/Alternate_history" title="Alternate history">alternate history</a> novels and series of novels with <a href="/wiki/William_R._Forstchen" title="William R. Forstchen">William R. Forstchen</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1945_(Gingrich_novel)" title="1945 (Gingrich novel)">1945</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Baen_Books" title="Baen Books">Baen Books</a>, August 1995; <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780671877392">ISBN 978-0-671-87739-2</a></li>
<li>Civil War series
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Gettysburg:_A_Novel_of_the_Civil_War" title="Gettysburg: A Novel of the Civil War">Gettysburg: A Novel of the Civil War</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Dunne_Books" title="Thomas Dunne Books">Thomas Dunne Books</a>, June 2003 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312309350">ISBN 978-0-312-30935-0</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Grant_Comes_East" title="Grant Comes East">Grant Comes East</a></i> Thomas Dunne Books, June 2004 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312309374">ISBN 978-0-312-30937-4</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Never_Call_Retreat:_Lee_and_Grant:_The_Final_Victory" title="Never Call Retreat: Lee and Grant: The Final Victory">Never Call Retreat: Lee and Grant: The Final Victory</a></i> Thomas Dunne Books, June 2005 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312342982">ISBN 978-0-312-34298-2</a></li>
<li><i>The Battle of the Crater: A Novel</i> Thomas Dunne Books, November 2011 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312607104">ISBN 978-0-312-60710-4</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pacific_War_series" title="Pacific War series">Pacific War series</a>
<ul>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor:_A_Novel_of_December_8" title="Pearl Harbor: A Novel of December 8">Pearl Harbor: A Novel of December 8</a></i> Thomas Dunne Books, May 2007 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312363505">ISBN 978-0-312-36350-5</a></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Days_of_Infamy_(Newt_Gingrich)" title="Days of Infamy (Newt Gingrich)">Days of Infamy</a></i> Thomas Dunne Books, April 2008 <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312363512">ISBN 978-0-312-36351-2</a></li>

<ul>

<li><i>Valley Forge: George Washington and the Crucible of Victory</i>, November 2010, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312591076">ISBN 978-0-312-59107-6</a></li>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Political and<br/>
legislative career</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
